<a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India"><img alt="Prime Minister of India" data-file-height="562" data-file-width="331" height="68" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Emblem_of_India.svg/40px-Emblem_of_India.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Emblem_of_India.svg/60px-Emblem_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Emblem_of_India.svg/80px-Emblem_of_India.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>

<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Narendra_Modi&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>

<p><b>Narendra Damodardas Modi</b> (<small>Gujarati: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Gujarati" title="Help:IPA for Gujarati">[ˈnəɾeːnd̪rə d̪aːmoːd̪əɾˈd̪aːs ˈmoːd̪iː]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Hi-NarendraModi.ogg" title="File:Hi-NarendraModi.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Hi-NarendraModi.ogg" title="Hi-NarendraModi.ogg">listen</a>)</small>, born 17 September 1950) is an Indian politician who is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_India" title="List of Prime Ministers of India">14th</a> and current <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India">Prime Minister of India</a>, in office since 26 May 2014. Modi, a leader of the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a> (BJP), was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gujarat" title="Chief Minister of Gujarat">Chief Minister</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> from 2001 to 2014, and is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament,_Lok_Sabha" title="Member of parliament, Lok Sabha">Member of Parliament</a> from <a href="/wiki/Varanasi_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Varanasi (Lok Sabha constituency)">Varanasi</a>.</p>
<p>Born to a Gujarati family in <a href="/wiki/Vadnagar" title="Vadnagar">Vadnagar</a>, Modi helped his father sell tea as a child, and later ran his own stall. He was introduced to the right-wing Hindu nationalist organisation <a href="/wiki/Rashtriya_Swayamsevak_Sangh" title="Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh">Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh</a> at the age of eight, beginning a long association with the organisation. He left home after graduating from school, partly because of an arranged marriage which he rejected. Modi traveled around India for two years, and visited a number of religious centres. He returned to Gujarat and moved to <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a> in 1969 or 1970. In 1971 he became a full-time worker for the RSS. During the <a href="/wiki/The_Emergency_(India)" title="The Emergency (India)">state of emergency</a> imposed across the country in 1975, Modi was forced to go into hiding. The <a href="/wiki/Rashtriya_Swayamsevak_Sangh" title="Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh">RSS</a> assigned him to the BJP in 1985, and he held several positions within the party hierarchy until 2001, rising to the rank of general secretary.</p>
<p>Modi was appointed chief minister of Gujarat in 2001, due to <a href="/wiki/Keshubhai_Patel" title="Keshubhai Patel">Keshubhai Patel</a>'s failing health and poor public image following the <a href="/wiki/2001_Gujarat_earthquake" title="2001 Gujarat earthquake">earthquake in Bhuj</a>. Modi was elected to the legislative assembly soon after. His administration has been considered complicit in the <a href="/wiki/2002_Gujarat_riots" title="2002 Gujarat riots">2002 Gujarat riots</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobbio_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bobbio-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Clash_Within_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Clash_Within-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shani_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shani-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buncombe_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Buncombe-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hattrick_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hattrick-5">[5]</a></sup> or otherwise criticized for its handling of it, although a court found no evidence to prosecute Modi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> His policies as chief minister, credited with encouraging economic growth, have received praise,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and several industrial projects were begun during his tenure. His administration has been criticised for failing to significantly improve health, poverty, and education indices in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buncombe_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Buncombe-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hattrick_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hattrick-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi led the BJP in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_general_election,_2014" title="Indian general election, 2014">2014 general election</a>, which gave the party a majority in the <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a>, the first time a single party had achieved this since 1984. Modi himself was elected to parliament from Varanasi. Since taking office, Modi's administration has encouraged foreign direct investment in the Indian economy, increased spending on infrastructure, and reduced spending on health and social welfare programs. Modi has encouraged efficiency in the bureaucracy, and centralized power through the abolition of the planning commission. Modi has begun a high-profile sanitation campaign, and loosened environmental and labor laws. A <a href="/wiki/Hindu_nationalism" title="Hindu nationalism">Hindu nationalist</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Rashtriya_Swayamsevak_Sangh" title="Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh">Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh</a> (RSS), Modi remains a controversial figure domestically and internationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buncombe_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Buncombe-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span></h2>
<p>Narendra Modi was born on 17 September 1950 to a family of grocers in <a href="/wiki/Vadnagar" title="Vadnagar">Vadnagar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mehsana_district" title="Mehsana district">Mehsana district</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a> (present-day Gujarat). He was the third of six children born to Damodardas Mulchand Modi (c.1915 - 1989) and Hiraben Modi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201413.2C_15.2C_74_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201413.2C_15.2C_74-15">[15]</a></sup> Modi's family belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Modh" title="Modh">Modh</a>-<a href="/wiki/Ghanchi" title="Ghanchi">Ghanchi</a>-<a href="/wiki/Teli" title="Teli">Teli</a> (oil-presser) community,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI_Modh-Ghanchi-Teli_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOI_Modh-Ghanchi-Teli-19">[19]</a></sup> which is categorised as an <a href="/wiki/Other_Backward_Class" title="Other Backward Class">Other Backward Class</a> by the Indian government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI_Modh-Ghanchi-Teli_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-TOI_Modh-Ghanchi-Teli-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a child, Modi helped his father sell tea at the Vadnagar railway station, and later ran a tea stall with his brother near a bus terminus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jose_Caravan_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jose_Caravan-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Modi completed his <a href="/wiki/Higher_Secondary_Examination" title="Higher Secondary Examination">higher secondary education</a> in Vadnagar in 1967, where a teacher described him as an average student and a keen debater, with an interest in theatre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jose_Caravan_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jose_Caravan-21">[21]</a></sup> Modi had an early gift for rhetoric in debates, and this was noted by his teachers and students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201416_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201416-23">[23]</a></sup> Modi preferred playing larger-than-life characters in theatrical productions, which has influenced his political image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay201382_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay201382-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_seeks_his_mother%27s_blessings_on_his_birthday_on_17th_sept.jpg"><img alt="Modi being fed by his mother" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Narendra_Modi_seeks_his_mother%27s_blessings_on_his_birthday_on_17th_sept.jpg/220px-Narendra_Modi_seeks_his_mother%27s_blessings_on_his_birthday_on_17th_sept.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Narendra_Modi_seeks_his_mother%27s_blessings_on_his_birthday_on_17th_sept.jpg/330px-Narendra_Modi_seeks_his_mother%27s_blessings_on_his_birthday_on_17th_sept.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Narendra_Modi_seeks_his_mother%27s_blessings_on_his_birthday_on_17th_sept.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_seeks_his_mother%27s_blessings_on_his_birthday_on_17th_sept.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi with his mother, Hiraben, on his 63rd birthday on 17 September 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At age eight, Modi discovered the <a href="/wiki/Rashtriya_Swayamsevak_Sangh" title="Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh">Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh</a> (RSS), and began attending its local <i>shakhas</i> (training sessions). There, Modi met <a href="/wiki/Lakshmanrao_Inamdar" title="Lakshmanrao Inamdar">Lakshmanrao Inamdar</a>, popularly known as Vakil Saheb, who inducted him as a <i>balswayamsevak</i> (junior cadet) for RSS and became his political mentor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201424_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201424-26">[26]</a></sup> While Modi was training with the RSS, he also met Vasant Gajendragadkar and Nathalal Jaghda, <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Jana_Sangh" title="Bharatiya Jana Sangh">Bharatiya Jana Sangh</a> leaders who were founding members of the BJP's Gujarat unit in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pathak_TNN_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pathak_TNN-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-new-india-express-_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-new-india-express--28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Engaged while still a child to a local girl, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jashodaben_Narendrabhai_Modi" title="Jashodaben Narendrabhai Modi">Jashodaben Narendrabhai Modi</a>, Modi rejected the arranged marriage at the same time he graduated from high school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201421_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201421-29">[29]</a></sup> The resulting familial tensions contributed to his decision to leave home in 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201422.E2.80.9323_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201422.E2.80.9323-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi spent the ensuing two years travelling across Northern and North-eastern India, though few details of where he went have emerged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201425_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201425-31">[31]</a></sup> In interviews, Modi has described visiting Hindu ashrams founded by <a href="/wiki/Swami_Vivekananda" title="Swami Vivekananda">Swami Vivekananda</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Belur_Math" title="Belur Math">Belur Math</a> near <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Advaita_Ashrama" title="Advaita Ashrama">Advaita Ashrama</a> in <a href="/wiki/Almora" title="Almora">Almora</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ramakrishna_Mission" title="Ramakrishna Mission">Ramakrishna Mission</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rajkot" title="Rajkot">Rajkot</a>. Modi remained only a short time at each, since he lacked the required college education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201430.E2.80.9333_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201430.E2.80.9333-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013128.E2.80.93129_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013128.E2.80.93129-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> "Modi's life is said to have Vivekananda's deep influence. People close to Modi have often been quoted, saying that Modi has molded many aspects of his life as Vivekananda's."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ts0716_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-ts0716-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Reaching the Belur Math in the early summer of 1968 and being turned away, Modi wandered through Calcutta, West Bengal and Assam, stopping by Siliguri and Guwahati.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201426_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201426-36">[36]</a></sup> Modi then went to the Ramakrishna Ashram in Almora, where he was again rejected, before travelling back to Gujarat via Delhi and Rajasthan in 1968–69.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201427_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201427-37">[37]</a></sup> Sometime in late 1969 or early 1970, Modi returned to Vadnagar for a brief visit before leaving again for <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201428.E2.80.9329_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201428.E2.80.9329-38">[38]</a></sup> There, Modi lived with his uncle, working in the latter's canteen at the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_State_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Gujarat State Road Transport Corporation">Gujarat State Road Transport Corporation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013131_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013131-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013138_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013138-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Ahmedabad, Modi renewed his acquaintance with Inamdar, who was based at Hedgewar Bhavan (RSS headquarters) in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vakilsaheb_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-vakilsaheb-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livemint-modi-growth_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-livemint-modi-growth-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201435_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201435-43">[43]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1971" title="Indo-Pakistani War of 1971">Indo-Pakistani War of 1971</a>, he stopped working for his uncle and became a full-time <i>pracharak</i> (campaigner) for the RSS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013138_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013138-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1978, Modi became an RSS <i>sambhag pracharak</i> (regional organiser), and received a degree in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_Science" title="Political Science">Political Science</a> after a <a href="/wiki/Distance_education#University_correspondence_courses" title="Distance education">distance-education</a> course from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delhi_University" title="Delhi University">Delhi University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IT13092013_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-IT13092013-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201448_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201448-45">[45]</a></sup> Five years later, he received a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts" title="Master of Arts">Master of Arts</a> degree in political science from <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_University" title="Gujarat University">Gujarat University</a> in 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_political_career.2C_1975.E2.80.932001">Early political career, 1975–2001</span></h2>
<p>On 26 June 1975, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/The_Emergency_(India)" title="The Emergency (India)">state of emergency</a> in India which lasted until 1977. During this period, many of her political opponents were jailed and opposition groups (including the RSS) were banned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuha2008493.E2.80.93494_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuha2008493.E2.80.93494-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKochanekHardgrave2007205_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKochanekHardgrave2007205-49">[49]</a></sup> As <i>pracharak in-charge</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Akhil_Bharatiya_Vidyarthi_Parishad" title="Akhil Bharatiya Vidyarthi Parishad">Akhil Bharatiya Vidyarthi Parishad</a> (ABVP), the student wing of the RSS, Modi was forced to go underground in Gujarat and frequently travelled in disguise to avoid arrest. He became involved in printing pamphlets opposing the government, sending them to Delhi and organising demonstrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jose_Caravan_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jose_Caravan-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201443_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201443-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013150_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013150-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rediff-7rcr_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-rediff-7rcr-52">[52]</a></sup> During this period, Modi wrote a book in <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>, <i>Sangharsh Ma Gujarat</i> (<i>In The Struggles of Gujarat</i>), describing events during the Emergency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aakar-PoetModi_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aakar-PoetModi-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was assigned by the RSS to the BJP in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pathak_TNN_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pathak_TNN-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1988, Modi was elected organising secretary of the party's Gujarat unit, marking his entrance into electoral politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IT13092013_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-IT13092013-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> He rose within the party, helping organise <a href="/wiki/L._K._Advani" title="L. K. Advani">L. K. Advani</a>'s 1990 <a href="/wiki/Ram_Rath_Yatra" title="Ram Rath Yatra">Ram Rath Yatra</a> in 1990 and <a href="/wiki/Murli_Manohar_Joshi" title="Murli Manohar Joshi">Murli Manohar Joshi</a>'s 1991–92 <i>Ekta Yatra</i> (Journey for Unity).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jose_Caravan_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jose_Caravan-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay201368.E2.80.9369_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay201368.E2.80.9369-56">[56]</a></sup> As party secretary, Modi's electoral strategy was considered central to BJP victory in the 1995 state assembly elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pathak_TNN_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-Pathak_TNN-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venkatesan_Frontline_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Venkatesan_Frontline-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In November of that year Modi was elected BJP national secretary and transferred to New Delhi, where he assumed responsibility for party activities in Haryana and <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venkatesan_Frontline_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Venkatesan_Frontline-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The following year, <a href="/wiki/Shankersinh_Vaghela" title="Shankersinh Vaghela">Shankersinh Vaghela</a> (one of the most prominent BJP leaders in Gujarat) defected to the INC after losing his parliamentary seat in the Lok Sabha elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jose_Caravan_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-Jose_Caravan-21">[21]</a></sup> Modi, on the selection committee for the 1998 Assembly elections in Gujarat, favoured supporters of BJP leader <a href="/wiki/Keshubhai_Patel" title="Keshubhai Patel">Keshubhai Patel</a> over those supporting Vaghela to end factional division in the party. His strategy was credited as key to the BJP winning an overall majority in the 1998 elections,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venkatesan_Frontline_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-Venkatesan_Frontline-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201478_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201478-60">[60]</a></sup> and Modi was promoted to BJP general secretary (organisation) in May of that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarino201479_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarino201479-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chief_Minister_of_Gujarat">Chief Minister of Gujarat</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taking_office">Taking office</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_(9123711411).jpg"><img alt="Modi flanked by three other men at a table" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="325" data-file-width="630" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_%289123711411%29.jpg/240px-Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_%289123711411%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_%289123711411%29.jpg/360px-Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_%289123711411%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_%289123711411%29.jpg/480px-Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_%289123711411%29.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shri_Modi_at_Planning_Commission_Meet_in_New_Delhi_(9123711411).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi and his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Gujarat" title="Council of Ministers of Gujarat">cabinet ministers</a> at a <a href="/wiki/Planning_Commission_(India)" title="Planning Commission (India)">Planning Commission</a> meeting in New Delhi, 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001, Keshubhai Patel's health was failing and the BJP lost a few state assembly seats in <a href="/wiki/By-election" title="By-election">by-elections</a>. Allegations of abuse of power, corruption and poor administration were made, and Patel's standing had been damaged by his administration's handling of the <a href="/wiki/2001_Gujarat_earthquake" title="2001 Gujarat earthquake">earthquake in Bhuj in 2001</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venkatesan_Frontline_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-Venkatesan_Frontline-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phadnis_BS_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Phadnis_BS-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The BJP national leadership sought a new candidate for chief minister, and Modi, who had expressed misgivings about Patel's administration, was chosen as a replacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jose_Caravan_21-5"><a href="#cite_note-Jose_Caravan-21">[21]</a></sup> Although senior BJP leader <a href="/wiki/L._K._Advani" title="L. K. Advani">L. K. Advani</a> did not want to ostracise Patel and was concerned about Modi's lack of experience in government, Modi declined an offer to be Patel's deputy chief minister, telling Advani and <a href="/wiki/Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee" title="Atal Bihari Vajpayee">Atal Bihari Vajpayee</a> that he was "going to be fully responsible for Gujarat or not at all". On 3 October 2001 he replaced Patel as Chief Minister of Gujarat, with the responsibility of preparing the BJP for the December 2002 elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On 7 October 2001, Modi was administered the oath of office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On 24 February 2002 he won a <a href="/wiki/By-election" title="By-election">by-election</a> to the Rajkot – II assembly constituency, defeating Ashwin Mehta of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> (INC) by 14,728 votes, which enabled him to take office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_Gujarat_riots">2002 Gujarat riots</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2002_Gujarat_riots" title="2002 Gujarat riots">2002 Gujarat riots</a></div>
<p>On 27 February 2002, a train with several hundred passengers was <a href="/wiki/Godhra_train_burning" title="Godhra train burning">burned near Godhra</a>, killing approximately 60 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[a]</a></sup> The train carried a large number of Hindu pilgrims returning from Ayodhya after a religious ceremony at the site of the demolished <a href="/wiki/Babri_Masjid" title="Babri Masjid">Babri Masjid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Communal_Riots_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Communal_Riots-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> In making a public statement after the incident, Modi said that the attack had been pre-planned terror attack by local Muslims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shani_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shani-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Communal_Riots_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Communal_Riots-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy_2010_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy_2010-72">[71]</a></sup> The next day, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vishwa_Hindu_Parishad" title="Vishwa Hindu Parishad">Vishwa Hindu Parishad</a> called for a <i><a href="/wiki/Bandh" title="Bandh">bandh</a></i> across the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curfew_imposed_in_26_cities_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curfew_imposed_in_26_cities-74">[73]</a></sup> Riots began during the <i>bandh</i>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Muslim_violence_in_India" title="Anti-Muslim violence in India">anti-Muslim violence</a> spread through Gujarat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Communal_Riots_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-Communal_Riots-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curfew_imposed_in_26_cities_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Curfew_imposed_in_26_cities-74">[73]</a></sup> The government's decision to move the bodies of the train victims from Godhra to Ahmedabad had the effect of further inflaming the violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Communal_Riots_70-3"><a href="#cite_note-Communal_Riots-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> The state government stated later that 790 Muslims and 254 Hindus were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> Independent sources put the death toll at over 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Communal_Riots_70-4"><a href="#cite_note-Communal_Riots-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Approximately 150,000 people were driven to refugee camps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brass_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brass-78">[77]</a></sup> Numerous women and children were among the victims; the violence included mass rapes and mutilations of women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Clash_Within_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Clash_Within-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government of Gujarat itself is generally considered by scholars to have been complicit in the riots,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobbio_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bobbio-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Clash_Within_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-The_Clash_Within-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shani_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Shani-3">[3]</a></sup> and has otherwise received heavy criticism for its handling of the situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-79">[78]</a></sup> Several scholars have described the violence as a <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">pogrom</a>, while others have called it an example of <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">state terrorism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pandey_2005_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pandey_2005-81">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baruah_2012_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baruah_2012-82">[81]</a></sup> Summarising academic views on the subject, <a href="/wiki/Martha_Nussbaum" title="Martha Nussbaum">Martha Nussbaum</a> said: "There is by now a broad consensus that the Gujarat violence was a form of ethnic cleansing, that in many ways it was premeditated, and that it was carried out with the complicity of the state government and officers of the law."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Clash_Within_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-The_Clash_Within-2">[2]</a></sup> The Modi government imposed a curfew in 26 major cities, issued shoot-at-sight orders and called for the army to patrol the streets, but was unable to prevent the violence from escalating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curfew_imposed_in_26_cities_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-Curfew_imposed_in_26_cities-74">[73]</a></sup> The president of the state unit of the BJP expressed support for the <i>bandh</i>, despite such actions being illegal at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shani_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Shani-3">[3]</a></sup> State officials later prevented riot victims from leaving the refugee camps, and the camps were often unable to meet the needs of those living there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hampton_2002_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hampton_2002-83">[82]</a></sup> Muslim victims of the riots were subject to further discrimination when the state government announced that compensation for Muslim victims would be half of that offered to Hindus, although this decision was later reversed after the issue was taken to court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_Model_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_Model-84">[83]</a></sup> During the riots, police officers often did not intervene in situations where they were able.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Clash_Within_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-The_Clash_Within-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy_2010_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy_2010-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_2002_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_2002-85">[84]</a></sup> In 2012 <a href="/wiki/Maya_Kodnani" title="Maya Kodnani">Maya Kodnani</a>, a minister in Modi's government from 2007 to 2009, was convicted of participation in the <a href="/wiki/Naroda_Patiya_massacre" title="Naroda Patiya massacre">Naroda Patiya massacre</a> during the 2002 riots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Although Modi's government had announced that it would seek the death penalty for Kodnani on appeal, it reversed its decision in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi's personal involvement in the 2002 events has continued to be debated. During the riots, Modi said that "What is happening is a chain of action and reaction."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Clash_Within_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-The_Clash_Within-2">[2]</a></sup> Later in 2002, Modi said the way in which he had handled the media was his only regret regarding the episode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> Modi has not offered an apology for the riots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stepan_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stepan-91">[90]</a></sup> In March 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_India" title="Supreme Court of India">Supreme Court</a> reopened several cases related to the 2002 riots, including that of the <a href="/wiki/Gulbarg_Society_massacre" title="Gulbarg Society massacre">Gulbarg Society massacre</a>, and established a Special Investigation Team (SIT) to look into the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-79">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZakiavsModi-timeline_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-ZakiavsModi-timeline-92">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHRCvsGujarat-2009-judgment_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHRCvsGujarat-2009-judgment-93">[92]</a></sup> In response to a petition from Zakia Jafri (widow of <a href="/wiki/Ehsan_Jafri" title="Ehsan Jafri">Ehsan Jafri</a>, who was killed in the Gulbarg Society massacre), in April 2009 the court also asked the SIT to investigate the issue of Modi's complicity in the killings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZakiavsModi-timeline_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-ZakiavsModi-timeline-92">[91]</a></sup> The SIT questioned Modi in March 2010; in May, it presented to the court a report finding no evidence against Modi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZakiavsModi-timeline_92-2"><a href="#cite_note-ZakiavsModi-timeline-92">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> In July 2011, the court-appointed <i><a href="/wiki/Amicus_curiae" title="Amicus curiae">amicus curiae</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Raju_Ramachandran" title="Raju Ramachandran">Raju Ramachandran</a> submitted his final report to the court. Contrary to the SIT's position, he said that Modi could be prosecuted based on the available evidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu-raju-report_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu-raju-report-95">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> The Supreme Court gave the matter to the magistrate court. The SIT examined Ramachandran's report, and in March 2012 submitted its final report, asking for the case to be closed. Zakia Jaffri filed a protest petition in response. In December 2013 the magistrate court rejected the protest petition, accepting the SIT's finding that there was no evidence against the chief minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013_Clean_chit_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Clean_chit-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_election">2002 election</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27,_2002.jpg"><img alt="Modi and former Prime Minister Vajpayee looking at a blue-covered report" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="609" data-file-width="900" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27%2C_2002.jpg/200px-Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27%2C_2002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27%2C_2002.jpg/300px-Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27%2C_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27%2C_2002.jpg/400px-Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27%2C_2002.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_and_Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee_on_March_27,_2002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi with Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee" title="Atal Bihari Vajpayee">Atal Bihari Vajpayee</a> in 2002.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the aftermath of the violence came widespread calls for Modi to resign as chief minister from within and outside the state, including leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Dravida_Munnetra_Kazhagam" title="Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam">Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_Desam_Party" title="Telugu Desam Party">Telugu Desam Party</a> (allies in the BJP-led <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Alliance_(India)" title="National Democratic Alliance (India)">National Democratic Alliance</a> coalition), and opposition parties stalled Parliament over the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Modi submitted his resignation, which was not accepted, at the April 2002 BJP national executive meeting in Goa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> His cabinet had a 19 July 2002 emergency meeting, offered its resignation to the Gujarat Governor S. S. Bhandari and the assembly was dissolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Despite opposition from the election commissioner, who said that a number of voters were still displaced, Modi succeeded in advancing the election to December 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_T.26NM_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_T.26NM-102">[101]</a></sup> In the elections, the BJP won 127 seats in the 182-member assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> Although Modi later denied it, he made significant use of anti-Muslim rhetoric during his campaign,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brasted_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brasted-105">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> and the BJP profited by the division of the vote along religious lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_T.26NM_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_T.26NM-102">[101]</a></sup> Modi hired the public relations firm <a href="/wiki/APCO_Worldwide" title="APCO Worldwide">APCO Worldwide</a> to manage his image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_T.26NM_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_T.26NM-102">[101]</a></sup> He won the Maninagar constituency, receiving 1,13,589 of 1,54,981 votes and defeating INC candidate Yatin Oza by 75,333 votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> On 22 December 2002, Bhandari swore Modi in for a second term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> Modi framed the criticism of his government for human rights violations as an attack upon Gujarati pride, a strategy which led to the BJP winning two-thirds of the seats in the state assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobbio_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bobbio-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi's public speeches during the election campaign had been focused on the 2002 riots, but after the election, the stated agenda of the government shifted toward economic development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobbio_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bobbio-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup> Modi organized a "Vibrant Gujarat" summit, where Gujarat was advertised as an attractive destination for private investment. During the summit, which would later become a biennial event, Modi offered financial incentives to investors, and also referred to Gujarat's culture as a factor which made the state well-suited for business. His rhetoric was aimed at a middle-class Hindu audience and sought to consolidate a Gujarati cultural identity based on upper-caste Hindu cultural elements. However, after the 2002 election the BJP reduced the use of anti-Muslim rhetoric in its campaigns in favour of statements about economic development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobbio_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-Bobbio-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_term">Second term</span></h3>
<p>After an election campaign in which the BJP benefited from religious polarisation among the voters, during Modi's second term the rhetoric of the government shifted from <a href="/wiki/Hindutva" title="Hindutva">Hindutva</a> to Gujarat's economic development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phadnis_BS_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-Phadnis_BS-62">[62]</a></sup> Modi curtailed the influence of <a href="/wiki/Sangh_Parivar" title="Sangh Parivar">Sangh Parivar</a> organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Kisan_Sangh" title="Bharatiya Kisan Sangh">Bharatiya Kisan Sangh</a> (BKS) and the <a href="/wiki/Vishva_Hindu_Parishad" title="Vishva Hindu Parishad">Vishva Hindu Parishad</a> (VHP),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Umat_TNN_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Umat_TNN-110">[109]</a></sup> entrenched in the state after the decline of Ahmedabad's textile industry,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phadnis_BS_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-Phadnis_BS-62">[62]</a></sup> and dropped <a href="/wiki/Gordhan_Zadafia" title="Gordhan Zadafia">Gordhan Zadafia</a> (an ally of former Sangh co-worker and VHP state chief <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Praveen_Togadia" title="Praveen Togadia">Praveen Togadia</a>) from his cabinet. When the BKS staged a farmers' demonstration Modi ordered their eviction from state-provided houses, and his decision to demolish 200 illegal temples in <a href="/wiki/Gandhinagar" title="Gandhinagar">Gandhinagar</a> deepened the rift with the VHP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Umat_TNN_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Umat_TNN-110">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Sangh organisations were no longer consulted or informed in advance about Modi's administrative decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Umat_TNN_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-Umat_TNN-110">[109]</a></sup> Nonetheless, Modi retained connections with some Hindu nationalists. Modi wrote a forward to a textbook by <a href="/wiki/Dinanath_Batra" title="Dinanath Batra">Dinanath Batra</a> released in 2014, which stated that ancient India possessed technologies including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Test-tube_babies" title="Test-tube babies">test-tube babies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-testtubes_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-testtubes-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi's relationship with Muslims continued to be criticised. Prime Minister Atal Bihari Vajpayee (who asked Modi for tolerance in the aftermath of the 2002 Gujarat violence and supported his resignation as chief minister)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> distanced himself, reaching out to North Indian Muslims before the <a href="/wiki/Indian_general_election,_2004" title="Indian general election, 2004">2004 Lok Sabha elections</a>. After the elections Vajpayee called the violence in Gujarat a reason for the BJP's electoral defeat and said it had been a mistake to leave Modi in office after the riots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TellisWills_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-TellisWills-116">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Questions about Modi's relationship with Muslims were also raised by many Western nations during his tenure as chief minister. Modi was barred from entering the United States under a provision of the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Nationality_Act_of_1965" title="Immigration and Nationality Act of 1965">Immigration and Nationality Act</a> banning violators of religious freedom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> the only person <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_barred_or_excluded_from_the_United_States" title="List of people barred or excluded from the United States">denied a US visa</a> under this provision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> The UK and the European Union refused to admit him because of what they saw as his role in the riots. As Modi rose to prominence in India, the UK<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> and the EU<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> lifted their bans in October 2012 and March 2013, respectively, and after his election as prime minister he was invited to Washington.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker-may14_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-may14-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the run-up to the 2007 assembly elections and the 2009 general election, the BJP ramped up its rhetoric on terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> On 18 July 2006, Modi criticised Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a> "... for his reluctance to revive anti-terror legislation" such as the 2002 <a href="/wiki/Prevention_of_Terrorism_Act,_2002" title="Prevention of Terrorism Act, 2002">Prevention of Terrorism Act</a>. He asked the national government to allow states to invoke tougher laws in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Mumbai_train_bombings" title="2006 Mumbai train bombings">2006 Mumbai blasts</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_India_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_India-125">[124]</a></sup> and demanded the execution of <a href="/wiki/Afzal_Guru" title="Afzal Guru">Afzal Guru</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> who was convicted of involvement in the <a href="/wiki/2001_Indian_Parliament_attack" title="2001 Indian Parliament attack">2001 Indian Parliament attack</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI20130210_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOI20130210-127">[126]</a></sup> After the November <a href="/wiki/2008_Mumbai_attacks" title="2008 Mumbai attacks">2008 Mumbai attacks</a> Modi held a meeting to discuss the security of Gujarat's 1,600-kilometre (990 mi)-long coastline, resulting in <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">government</a> authorisation of 30 high-speed surveillance boats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> In July 2007 Modi completed 2,063 consecutive days as chief minister of Gujarat, making him the longest-serving holder of that post,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> and the BJP won 122 of 182 state-assembly seats in that year's election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_projects">Development projects</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006,_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006%2C_India.jpg/220px-Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006%2C_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006%2C_India.jpg/330px-Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006%2C_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006%2C_India.jpg/440px-Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006%2C_India.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sardar_Sarovar_Dam_2006,_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Sardar_Sarovar_Dam" title="Sardar Sarovar Dam">Sardar Sarovar Dam</a> during a 2006 height increase.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg"><img alt="Modi unties a ceremonial red ribbon before a crowd of onlookers" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="403" data-file-width="630" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg/220px-Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg/330px-Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg/440px-Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_inaugurates_Reliable_Hospital_in_Kheda_district.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi at a hospital dedication in <a href="/wiki/Kheda_district" title="Kheda district">Kheda district</a> in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As Chief Minister, Modi favoured privatisation and <a href="/wiki/Small_government" title="Small government">small government</a>, which was at odds with the philosophy of the RSS, usually described as anti-privatisation and anti-globalisation. His policies during his second term have been credited with reducing corruption in the state. He established financial and technology parks in Gujarat and during the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Vibrant_Gujarat" title="Vibrant Gujarat">Vibrant Gujarat</a> summit, real-estate investment deals worth <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>6.6 trillion were signed in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phadnis_BS_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-Phadnis_BS-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The governments led by Patel and Modi supported NGOs and communities in the creation of groundwater-conservation projects. By December 2008 500,000 structures had been built, of which 113,738 were <a href="/wiki/Check_dam" title="Check dam">check dams</a>, which helped recharge the <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifers</a> beneath them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_BS_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_BS-131">[130]</a></sup> Sixty of the 112 <a href="/wiki/Tehsil" title="Tehsil">tehsils</a> which had depleted the <a href="/wiki/Water_table" title="Water table">water table</a> in 2004 had regained their normal groundwater levels by 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> As a result, the state's production of genetically modified <a href="/wiki/Bt_cotton" title="Bt cotton">genetically modified cotton</a> increased to become the largest in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_BS_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_BS-131">[130]</a></sup> The boom in cotton production and its semi-arid land use<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farm_growth_Hindu_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farm_growth_Hindu-133">[132]</a></sup> led to Gujarat's agricultural growing at an average rate of 9.6 percent from 2001 to 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> Public irrigation measures in central and southern Gujarat, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sardar_Sarovar_Dam" title="Sardar Sarovar Dam">Sardar Sarovar Dam</a>, were less successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_BS_131-2"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_BS-131">[130]</a></sup> The Sardar Sarovar project only irrigated 4–6% of the area it was supposed to.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_BS_131-3"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_BS-131">[130]</a></sup> Nonetheless, from 2001 to 2010 Gujarat recorded an agricultural <a href="/wiki/Compound_annual_growth_rate" title="Compound annual growth rate">growth rate</a> of 10.97 percent – the highest of any state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farm_growth_Hindu_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-Farm_growth_Hindu-133">[132]</a></sup> However, sociologists have pointed out that the growth rate under the 1992–97 INC government was 12.9 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Business_Standard_Vibrant_Gujarat_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Standard_Vibrant_Gujarat-135">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008 Modi offered land in Gujarat to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> to set up a plant manufacturing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nano_(car)" title="Nano (car)">Nano</a> after after a popular agitation had forced the company to move out of West Bengal. Several other companies followed the Tata's to Gujarat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modi-nomics_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Modi-nomics-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Modi government completed the process of bringing electricity to every village in Gujarat, which had been nearly completed under the previous administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Business_Standard_Vibrant_Gujarat_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Standard_Vibrant_Gujarat-135">[134]</a></sup> Modi significantly changed the state's system of power distribution, greatly impacting farmers. Gujarat expanded the <a href="/wiki/Jyotigram_Yojana" title="Jyotigram Yojana">Jyotigram Yojana</a> scheme, in which agricultural electricity was separated from other rural electricity; the agricultural electricity was rationed to fit scheduled irrigation demands, reducing its cost. Although early protests by farmers ended when those who benefited found that their electricity supply had stabilised,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_BS_131-4"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_BS-131">[130]</a></sup> according to an assessment study corporations and large farmers benefited from the policy at the expense of small farmers and labourers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_2008_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_2008-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_debate">Development debate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Modi_at_GNLU.jpg"><img alt="Modi speaking at flower-decked podium" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="636" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Modi_at_GNLU.jpg/180px-Modi_at_GNLU.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Modi_at_GNLU.jpg/270px-Modi_at_GNLU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Modi_at_GNLU.jpg/360px-Modi_at_GNLU.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Modi_at_GNLU.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi addressing graduates of the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_National_Law_University" title="Gujarat National Law University">Gujarat National Law University</a> in 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There has been a contentious debate surrounding the development of the state of Gujarat during Modi's tenure as chief minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup> The GDP growth rate of Gujarat averaged 10% during Modi's tenure, a value above that of the country as a whole, and similar to other highly industrialised states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modi-nomics_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-Modi-nomics-136">[135]</a></sup> Gujarat also had a high rate of economic growth in the 1990s, before Modi took office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghatak_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ghatak-139">[138]</a></sup> Some scholars have stated the rate of growth did not accelerate during Modi's tenure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghatak_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ghatak-139">[138]</a></sup> although the state is considered to have maintained a high growth rate during Modi's Chief Ministership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_Model_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_Model-84">[83]</a></sup> Under Modi, Gujarat topped the World Bank's "ease of doing business" rankings among Indian states for two consecutive years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> In 2013, Gujarat was ranked first among Indian states for "economic freedom" by a report measuring governance, growth, citizens' rights and labour and business regulation among the country's 20 largest states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modi-nomics_136-2"><a href="#cite_note-Modi-nomics-136">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> In the later years of Modi's government, Gujarat's economic growth was frequently used as an argument to counter allegations of communalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobbio_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-Bobbio-1">[1]</a></sup> Tax breaks for businesses were easier to obtain in Gujarat than in other states, as was land. Modi's policies to make Gujarat attractive for investment included the creation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones" title="Special Economic Zones">Special Economic Zones</a>, where labor laws were greatly weakened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-3"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite its growth rate, Gujarat had a relatively poor record on human development, poverty relief, nutrition and education during Modi's tenure. In 2013, Gujarat ranked 13th in the country with respect to rates of poverty and 21st in education. Nearly 45 percent of children under five were underweight and 23 percent were undernourished, putting the state in the "alarming" category on the <a href="/wiki/India_State_Hunger_Index" title="India State Hunger Index">India State Hunger Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hariss_2015_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hariss_2015-143">[142]</a></sup> A study by <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> and the Indian government found that Gujarat under Modi had a poor record with respect to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immunisation" title="Immunisation">immunisation</a> in children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist_2015_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economist_2015-144">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the decade from 2001 to 2011, Gujarat did not change its position relative to the rest of the country with respect to poverty and female literacy, remaining near the median of the 29 Indian states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_Model_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_Model-84">[83]</a></sup> It showed only a marginal improvement in rates of infant mortality, and its position with respect to individual consumption declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_Model_84-3"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_Model-84">[83]</a></sup> With respect to the quality of education in government schools, the state ranked below most Indian states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_Model_84-4"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_Model-84">[83]</a></sup> The social policies of the government generally did not benefit Muslims, <a href="/wiki/Dalit" title="Dalit">Dalits</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adivasi" title="Adivasi">Adivasis</a>, and generally increased social inequalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_Model_84-5"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_Model-84">[83]</a></sup> Under Modi, the state government spent far less than the national average on education and healthcare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gujarat_Model_84-6"><a href="#cite_note-Gujarat_Model-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Development in Gujarat was generally limited to the urban middle class, and citizens in rural areas or from lower castes were increasingly marginalised. In 2013 the state ranked 10th of 21 Indian states in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. Political Scientist <a href="/wiki/Christophe_Jaffrelot" title="Christophe Jaffrelot">Christophe Jaffrelot</a> says that under Modi the number of families below the poverty line has increased and conditions for rural <a href="/wiki/Adivasi" title="Adivasi">adivasi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dalit" title="Dalit">dalits</a>, in particular, have declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot2013_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot2013-145">[144]</a></sup> In July 2013 economics Nobel Laureate <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a> expressed disapproval of Modi's governance record, saying that under his administration Gujarat's "record in education and healthcare is pretty bad".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AS1_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-AS1-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, economists <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Panagariya" title="Arvind Panagariya">Arvind Panagariya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jagdish_Bhagwati" title="Jagdish Bhagwati">Jagdish Bhagwati</a> say that Gujarat's social indicators have improved from a lower baseline than that of other Indian states. According to them, Gujarat's performance in raising <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rates has been superior to other states and the "rapid" improvement of health indicators is evidence that "its progress has not been poor by any means."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myths_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-myths-147">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_years">Final years</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg"><img alt="Modi talking to a woman; both are seated." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="684" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg/220px-Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg/330px-Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg/440px-Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_and_Anandiben_Patel_at_the_meeting_of_BJP_MLAs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi with <a href="/wiki/Anandiben_Patel" title="Anandiben Patel">Anandiben Patel</a> at a meeting of BJP MLAs after his election as prime minister; Patel succeeded him as Gujarat chief minister.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Legislative_Assembly_election,_2012" title="Gujarat Legislative Assembly election, 2012">Gujarat Legislative Assembly election, 2012</a></div>
<p>During the 2012 campaign, Modi attempted to identify himself with the state of Gujarat, a strategy similar to that used by <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a> during the <a href="/wiki/The_Emergency_(India)" title="The Emergency (India)">Emergency</a>, and projected himself as protecting Gujarat against persecution by the rest of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-4"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the BJP's shift away from explicit Hindutva, Modi's election campaign in 2007 and 2012 contained elements of Hindu nationalism. Modi only attended Hindu religious ceremonies, and had prominent associations with Hindu religious leaders. During his 2012 campaign he twice refused to wear articles of clothing gifted by Muslim leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-5"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup> He did, however, maintain relations with <a href="/wiki/Dawoodi_Bohra" title="Dawoodi Bohra">Dawoodi Bohra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-6"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup> His campaign included references to issues known to cause religious polarization, including to <a href="/wiki/Afzal_Guru" title="Afzal Guru">Afzal Guru</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Sohrabuddin_Sheikh" title="Death of Sohrabuddin Sheikh">killing of Sohrabuddin Sheikh</a>. The BJP did not nominate any Muslim candidates for the assembly election of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_Review_104-7"><a href="#cite_note-India_Review-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>While campaigning for the 2012 assembly elections, Modi made extensive use of holograms and other technologies allowing him to reach a large number of people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_T.26NM_102-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_T.26NM-102">[101]</a></sup> something he would repeat in the 2014 general election. In the 2012 Gujarat Legislative Assembly elections, Modi won the constituency of Maninagar by 86,373 votes over Shweta Bhatt, the INC candidate and wife of <a href="/wiki/Sanjiv_Bhatt" title="Sanjiv Bhatt">Sanjiv Bhatt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> The BJP won 115 of the 182 seats, continuing its majority during his tenure<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> and allowing the party to form the government (as it had in Gujarat since 1995).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SL-20121220_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-SL-20121220-150">[149]</a></sup> In later by-elections the BJP won four more assembly seats and two Lok Sabha seats held by the INC, although Modi did not campaign for its candidates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Wharton_India_Economic_Forum" title="Wharton India Economic Forum">Wharton India Economic Forum</a> (WIEF) at the <a href="/wiki/Wharton_School_of_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania">Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania</a> cancelled a keynote video-conference speech by Modi following protests by Indian-Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> After his election as prime minister, Modi resigned as the chief minister and as an MLA from <a href="/wiki/Maninagar" title="Maninagar">Maninagar</a> on 21 May 2014. <a href="/wiki/Anandiben_Patel" title="Anandiben Patel">Anandiben Patel</a> succeeded him as the chief minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Indian_general_election">2014 Indian general election</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party_campaign_for_Indian_general_election,_2014" title="Bharatiya Janata Party campaign for Indian general election, 2014">Bharatiya Janata Party campaign for Indian general election, 2014</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg"><img alt="Modi addressing a large crowd from a podium" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="630" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg/220px-Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg/330px-Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg/440px-Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_addressing_Vijay_Shankhnad_Rally_in_Meerut.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi addressing a rally in <a href="/wiki/Meerut" title="Meerut">Meerut</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Indian_general_election,_2014" title="Indian general election, 2014">2014 general election campaign</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 31 March 2013 Modi was appointed to the BJP parliamentary board, the highest decision-making body in the party,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> and at a meeting of the party's national executive on 9 June he was appointed chair of the BJP's central election campaign committee for the 2014 general election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chhibber_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chhibber-156">[155]</a></sup> BJP founding member <a href="/wiki/L._K._Advani" title="L. K. Advani">L. K. Advani</a> resigned his party posts after the appointment, citing concern with leaders who were "concerned with their personal agendas". His resignation, which was described as being a protest against Modi's elevation, was withdrawn the following day at the urging of RSS chief <a href="/wiki/Mohan_Bhagwat" title="Mohan Bhagwat">Mohan Bhagwat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> In September 2013, the BJP announced that the chief minister would be their candidate for prime minister in the 2014 Lok Sabha election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chhibber_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chhibber-156">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Other BJP leaders also initially expressed opposition to Modi's candidature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup> Modi's nomination also drew attention for his reputation as "one of contemporary India's most controversial and divisive politicians."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi played a dominant role in the BJP's 2009 general-election campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T.26NM_2015_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-T.26NM_2015-160">[159]</a></sup> Several people who voted for the BJP stated that if Modi had not been the prime-ministerial candidate, they would have voted for another party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup> The BJP projected an image of Modi as a strong, masculine leader, who would be able to take difficult decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-2"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chhibber_156-2"><a href="#cite_note-Chhibber-156">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> The focus on Modi as an individual was unusual for a BJP election campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-4"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> The election was described as a referendum on Narendra Modi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-3"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the campaign, Modi focused on the corruption scandals under the previous INC government, and played on his image as a politician who had created a high rate of GDP growth in Gujarat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-4"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-5"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup> Modi projected himself as a person who could bring about "development," without focus on any specific policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-6"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup> His message found support among young Indians and among middle-class citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-5"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup> The BJP under Modi was able to downplay concerns about the protection of religious minorities and Modi's commitment to <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secularism</a>, areas in which he had previously received criticism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-6"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup> Prior to the election Modi's image in the media had centered around his role in the 2002 Gujarat riots, but during the campaign the BJP was able to shift this to a focus on Modi's neoliberal ideology and the Gujarat model of development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T.26NM_2015_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-T.26NM_2015-160">[159]</a></sup> Although the BJP avoided issues of Hindu nationalism to an extent, Hindutva remained a significant part of its campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-7"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-2"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ganguly_2014_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ganguly_2014-164">[163]</a></sup> Through the campaign, the BJP received significantly more positive media coverage than its competitors, particularly in the northern and western parts of the country. Commentators attributed this to Modi's influence in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barclay_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barclay-165">[164]</a></sup> The campaign also made extensive use of advertising in vernacular media sources, portraying Modi as the victim of a "news media conspiracy" among the English language sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T.26NM_2015_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-T.26NM_2015-160">[159]</a></sup> However, the BJP's campaign was assisted by its wide influence in the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hariss_2015_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hariss_2015-143">[142]</a></sup> Modi's campaign blitz cost approximately INR 5000 crores ($830 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-7"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup> and received extensive financial support from corporate donors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hariss_2015_143-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hariss_2015-143">[142]</a></sup> In addition to more conventional campaign methods, such as rallies and the use of print media, Modi also made extensive use of social media,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-8"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-8"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup> and addressed more than 1000 rallies via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hologram" title="Hologram">hologram</a> appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ganguly_2014_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ganguly_2014-164">[163]</a></sup> The election was described as "India's first social media election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wpSocialMedia_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-wpSocialMedia-166">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The BJP won 31% of the vote,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stepan_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stepan-91">[90]</a></sup> and more than doubled its tally in the <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a> to 282, and became the first party to win a majority of seats on its own since 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T.26NM_2015_160-3"><a href="#cite_note-T.26NM_2015-160">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-3"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup> The results were described as a pro-Modi "wave."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-9"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-4"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup> Voter unhappiness with the INC, as well as with regional parties in North India, was another reason for the success of the BJP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-5"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup> The support network of the RSS played a role in Modi's success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-9"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup> Scholars studying the election also stated that Modi had an ability to attract supporters who would campaign for him, thus strengthening his
