position as a candidate but making the party's victory relatively fragile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jaffrelot_2015_154-10"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffrelot_2015-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chhibber_156-3"><a href="#cite_note-Chhibber-156">[155]</a></sup> In states such as Uttar Pradesh in which the BJP performed well, it drew exceptionally high support from upper-caste Hindus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-6"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup> It won only 10 percent of the Muslim vote, which was nonetheless more than it had won before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-7"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup> It performed particularly well in parts of the country that had recently experienced violence between Hindus and Muslims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-8"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>The magnitude of the BJP's victory led many commentators to say that the election constituted a political realignment away from progressive parties and towards the right-wing BJP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_2014_138-10"><a href="#cite_note-Basu_2014-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chacko_161-9"><a href="#cite_note-Chacko-161">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> Modi's tweet announcing his victory in the election was the most re-tweeted in India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaur_2015_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kaur_2015-169">[168]</a></sup> and was described as being emblematic of the political realignment away from a <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Nehruvian</a> secular, socialist state towards capitalism and <a href="/wiki/Hindutva" title="Hindutva">Hindu cultural nationalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaur_2015_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kaur_2015-169">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi himself was a candidate for the Lok Sabha in two constituencies: Varanasi and <a href="/wiki/Vadodara_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Vadodara (Lok Sabha constituency)">Vadodara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> He won in both constituencies, defeating <a href="/wiki/Aam_Aadmi_Party" title="Aam Aadmi Party">Aam Aadmi Party</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Kejriwal" title="Arvind Kejriwal">Arvind Kejriwal</a> in Varanasi and <a href="/wiki/Madhusudan_Mistry" title="Madhusudan Mistry">Madhusudan Mistry</a> of the INC in Vadodara by 570,128 votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> The BJP-led NDA won the general election overall and the INC experienced its worst-ever defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> Modi, who was unanimously elected leader of the BJP after his party's victory, was appointed prime minister by India's president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-appointment-prez_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-appointment-prez-175">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-appointment-IE_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-appointment-IE-176">[175]</a></sup> To comply with the law that an MP cannot represent more than one constituency, he vacated the Vadodara seat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prime_Minister">Prime Minister</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Premiership_of_Narendra_Modi" title="Premiership of Narendra Modi">Premiership of Narendra Modi</a></div>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/BJP%27s_Narendra_Modi_elected_new_prime_minister_of_India" title="wikinews:BJP's Narendra Modi elected new prime minister of India">Narendra Modi elected new Prime Minister of India.</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg"><img alt="Modi reading from a paper into a bank of microphones" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="684" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg/220px-Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg/330px-Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg/440px-Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shri_Narendra_Modi_sworn_in_as_Prime_Minister.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi (<i>far right</i>) being sworn in as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India">Prime Minister</a>, in the presence of <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Pranab_Mukherjee" title="Pranab Mukherjee">Pranab Mukherjee</a> (<i>far left</i>), 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Modi was <a href="/wiki/Swearing-in_ceremony_of_Narendra_Modi" title="Swearing-in ceremony of Narendra Modi">sworn in as the Prime Minister of India</a> on 26 May 2014 at the <a href="/wiki/Rashtrapati_Bhavan" title="Rashtrapati Bhavan">Rashtrapati Bhavan</a>. He became the first Prime Minister born after India's <a href="/wiki/Indian_Independence_Act_1947" title="Indian Independence Act 1947">independence</a> from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI-20140520_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOI-20140520-178">[177]</a></sup> His first cabinet consisted of 45 ministers, 25 fewer than the previous UPA government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> 21 new ministers were added to the council of ministers in November 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_policies">Economic policies</span></h3>
<p>The economic policies of Modi's government focused on privatisation and liberalisation of the economy, based on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> framework.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_.26_Lerche_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_.26_Lerche-181">[180]</a></sup> Modi liberalised India's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> policies, allowing more foreign investment in several industries, including in defence and the railways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> Other reforms included removing many of the country's labor laws, to make it harder for workers to form unions and easier for employers to hire and fire them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_.26_Lerche_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_.26_Lerche-181">[180]</a></sup> These reforms met with support from institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, but opposition from scholars within the country. The labour laws also drew strong opposition from unions: on 2 September 2015, eleven of the country's largest unions went on strike, including one affiliated with the BJP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_.26_Lerche_181-2"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_.26_Lerche-181">[180]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Mazdoor_Sangh" title="Bharatiya Mazdoor Sangh">Bharatiya Mazdoor Sangh</a>, a constituent of the Sangh Parivar, stated that the reforms would hurt laborers by making it easier for corporations to exploit them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> In his first budget, Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Arun_Jaitley" title="Arun Jaitley">Arun Jaitley</a> promised to gradually reduce the budgetary deficit from 4.1% to 3% over two years, and to divest from shares in public banks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> Over Modi's first year in office, the Indian GDP grew at a rate of 7.5%, making it the fastest growing large economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shah_.26_Lerche_181-3"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_.26_Lerche-181">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>The funds dedicated to poverty reduction programs and social welfare measures was greatly decreased by the Modi administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> The money spent on social programs declined from 14.6% of GDP during the Congress government to 12.6% during Modi's first year in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-5"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> Spending on health and family welfare declined by 15%, and on primary and secondary education, by 16%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-6"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> The budgetary allocation for the <a href="/wiki/Sarva_Shiksha_Abhiyan" title="Sarva Shiksha Abhiyan">Sarva Shiksha Abhiyan</a>, or the "education for all" program, declined by 22%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-7"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> The government also lowered corporate taxes, abolished the wealth tax, and reduced customs duties on gold, jewelry, and increased sales taxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-8"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> In October 2014, the Modi government deregulated diesel prices,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> and later increased taxes on diesel and petrol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-9"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="306" data-file-width="684" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg/220px-Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg/330px-Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg/440px-Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_launches_Make_in_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi at the launch of the <i><a href="/wiki/Make_in_India" title="Make in India">Make in India</a></i> program.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In September 2014, Modi introduced the <a href="/wiki/Make_in_India" title="Make in India">Make in India</a> initiative to encourage foreign companies to manufacture products in India, with the goal of turning India into a global manufacturing hub.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-10"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> Supporters of economic liberalisation supported the initiative, while critics argued it would allow foreign corporations to capture a greater share of the Indian market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-11"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> In order to enable the construction of private industrial corridors, the Modi administration passed a land-reform bill that allowed it to acquire private agricultural land without conducting a social impact assessment, and without the consent of the farmers who owned it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup> Under the previous bill, the government had required the consent of 80% of the owners of a piece of property before acquiring it for a private project: this requirement was waived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronojoy_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ronojoy-188">[187]</a></sup> The bill was passed via an executive order after it faced opposition in parliament, but was eventually allowed to lapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronojoy_188-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ronojoy-188">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 June 2015, Modi launched a program intended to develop 100 <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart cities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SmartCity_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-SmartCity-189">[188]</a></sup> The "Smart Cities" program is expected to bring IT companies an extra benefit of 20,000,000,000 rupees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaushik_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kaushik-190">[189]</a></sup> In June 2015, Modi launched the "<a href="/wiki/Housing_for_All" title="Housing for All">Housing for All</a> By 2022" project, which intends to eliminate <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a> in India by building about 20 million affordable homes for India's urban poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his first cabinet decision, Modi set up a team to investigate black money.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> On 9 November 2016, the government <a href="/wiki/2016_Indian_banknote_demonetisation" title="2016 Indian banknote demonetisation">demonetised ₹500 and ₹1000 banknotes</a>, with the stated intention of curbing corruption, black money, the use of counterfeit currency, and terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> The move led to widespread protests throughout the country, including one by opposition parties, which stalled the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2016_winter_session_of_Indian_Parliament_and_debate_on_note_ban" title="2016 winter session of Indian Parliament and debate on note ban">winter session of parliament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> In the days following the demonetisation, banks across the country faced severe cash shortages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> which had detrimental effects on a number of small businesses, on agriculture, and on transportation. People seeking to exchange their notes had lengthy waits, and several deaths were linked to the rush to exchange cash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aljazeera-1_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aljazeera-1-199">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> Following Modi's announcement, the Indian stock indices <a href="/wiki/BSE_SENSEX" title="BSE SENSEX">BSE SENSEX</a> and <a href="/wiki/NIFTY_50" title="NIFTY 50">NIFTY 50</a> declined steeply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_sanitation_policies">Health and sanitation policies</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Swachh_Bharat_Abhiyan" title="Swachh Bharat Abhiyan">Swachh Bharat Abhiyan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat,_Varanasi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="584" data-file-width="684" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat%2C_Varanasi.jpg/220px-PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat%2C_Varanasi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat%2C_Varanasi.jpg/330px-PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat%2C_Varanasi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat%2C_Varanasi.jpg/440px-PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat%2C_Varanasi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PM_Modi_participates_in_Shramdaan_as_part_of_Swachhta_Abhiyan_at_Assi_Ghat,_Varanasi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi participates in the cleanliness drive in his constituency of <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In his first year as prime minister Modi reduced the amount of money spent by the government on healthcare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist_2015_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-Economist_2015-144">[143]</a></sup> His Modi government launched a "New Health Policy" in January 2015, although this did not increase the government's spending on healthcare but rather placed emphasis on the role of private healthcare organisations. This represented a shift away from the policy of the previous Congress government, which had supported programs to assist public health goals, including reducing child and maternal mortality rates. The National Health Mission, which included public health programs targeted at these indices received nearly 25% less funds in 2015 than in the previous year. 15 national health programs, including those aimed at controlling tobacco use and supporting healthcare for the elderly, were merged with the National Health Mission, and received less funds than in previous years. Modi initially appointed <a href="/wiki/Harsh_Vardhan_(Delhi_politician)" title="Harsh Vardhan (Delhi politician)">Harsh Vardhan</a>, a doctor and an advocate of tobacco control, as minister of health. However, Vardhan was removed in November 2015. The government also proposed introducing stricter packaging laws for tobacco, but this effort was postponed because of the efforts of the tobacco lobby. In its budget for the second year after it took office, the Modi government reduced healthcare spending by 15%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet-202">[201]</a></sup> Modi has generally emphasized his government's efforts at sanitation as a means of ensuring good health. An article in the medical journal <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lancet" title="The Lancet">Lancet</a></i> stated that the country "might have taken a few steps back in public health" under Modi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet-202">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 October 2014, Modi launched the <a href="/wiki/Swachh_Bharat_Abhiyan" title="Swachh Bharat Abhiyan">Swachh Bharat Abhiyan</a> ("Clean India") campaign. The states goals of the campaign included eliminating <a href="/wiki/Open_defecation" title="Open defecation">open defecation</a>, eliminating <a href="/wiki/Manual_scavenging" title="Manual scavenging">manual scavenging</a>, and improving waste management practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clean_India_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clean_India-204">[203]</a></sup> The plann was to achieve these aims in five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clean_India_204-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clean_India-204">[203]</a></sup> As part of the programme, the Indian government began the construction of millions toilets in rural areas, as well as efforts to encourage people to use them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lakshmi_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lakshmi-205">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gahlot_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gahlot-206">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> The government also announced plans to build new sewage treatment plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> The administration plans to construct 60 million toilets by 2019. The construction projects have faced allegations of corruption, and have faced severe difficulty in getting people to use the toilets constructed for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clean_India_204-2"><a href="#cite_note-Clean_India-204">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lakshmi_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lakshmi-205">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gahlot_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gahlot-206">[205]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindutva_and_education_policy">Hindutva and education policy</span></h3>
<p>During the 2014 election campaign, the BJP sought to identify itself with political leaders known to have opposed <a href="/wiki/Hindu_nationalism" title="Hindu nationalism">Hindu nationalism</a>, including <a href="/wiki/B._R._Ambedkar" title="B. R. Ambedkar">B. R. Ambedkar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subhas_Chandra_Bose" title="Subhas Chandra Bose">Subhas Chandra Bose</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ram_Manohar_Lohia" title="Ram Manohar Lohia">Ram Manohar Lohia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-2"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> The campaign also saw the use of rhetoric based on Hindutva, however, by BJP leaders in certain states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palshikar_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Palshikar-209">[208]</a></sup> Communal tensions were played upon especially in Uttar Pradesh and the states of Northeast India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palshikar_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-Palshikar-209">[208]</a></sup> A proposal for the controversial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uniform_Civil_Code" title="Uniform Civil Code">Uniform Civil Code</a> was a part of the BJP's election manifesto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ganguly_2014_164-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ganguly_2014-164">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several state governments headed by the BJP have enacted policies aligned with Hindutva after the election of Modi as prime minister. The government of Maharashtra banned the killing of cows in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palshikar_209-2"><a href="#cite_note-Palshikar-209">[208]</a></sup> The Modi administration has generally avoided directly supporting policies related to a Hindutva agenda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palshikar_209-3"><a href="#cite_note-Palshikar-209">[208]</a></sup> There has been an increase in the activities of a number of other Hindu nationalist organisations, sometimes with the support of the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-3"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palshikar_209-4"><a href="#cite_note-Palshikar-209">[208]</a></sup> The incidents included a campaign against "<a href="/wiki/Love_Jihad" title="Love Jihad">Love Jihad</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Ghar_Wapsi" title="Ghar Wapsi">religious conversion</a> programme, and attempts to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Nathuram_Godse" title="Nathuram Godse">Nathuram Godse</a>, the assassin of <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>, by members of the <a href="/wiki/Sangh_Parivar" title="Sangh Parivar">Sangh Parivar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-4"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> The attempts at religious conversion have been described by the VHP and other organisations involved with them as attempts at "reconversion" from Islam or Christianity. There have been a number of reports of intimidation or coercion of the subjects during these attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palshikar_209-5"><a href="#cite_note-Palshikar-209">[208]</a></sup> Officials in the government, including the Home Minister, have defended the attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palshikar_209-6"><a href="#cite_note-Palshikar-209">[208]</a></sup> There were additional incidents of violence targeted at religious minorities by Hindu nationalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-5"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> Modi refused to remove a government minister from her position after a popular outcry resulted from her referring to religious minorities as "bastards."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-6"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> Commentators have suggested, however, that the violence was perpetrated by radical Hindu nationalists to undercut the authority of Modi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-7"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Modi administration appointed <a href="/wiki/Yellapragada_Sudershan_Rao" title="Yellapragada Sudershan Rao">Yellapragada Sudershan Rao</a>, who had previously been associated with the RSS, chairperson of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Council_of_Historical_Research" title="Indian Council of Historical Research">Indian Council of Historical Research</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ganguly_2014_164-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ganguly_2014-164">[163]</a></sup> In reaction to his appointment, other historians and former members of the ICHR, including those sympathetic to the ruling party, questioned his credentials as a historian. Several stated that the appointment was part of an agenda of cultural nationalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ganguly_2014_164-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ganguly_2014-164">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saffronisation_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-saffronisation-210">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-right_wing_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-right_wing-211">[210]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government began formulating a New Education Policy, or NEP, soon after its election. As of March 2016, this policy had yet to be implemented. This was the third education policy introduced by the Indian government, following those of 1968 and 1986. The policy was described as having overtones of Hindutva. The RSS had a role in its creation, and it did not explicitly mention the goals of "socialism, secularism and democracy" that had been mentioned in the first two policies. The policy emphasised the education of minority students, as well as those of economically backward groups, in particular on improving enrolment in schools among those groups. The policy proposed bringing religious educational institutions under the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_Children_to_Free_and_Compulsory_Education_Act" title="Right of Children to Free and Compulsory Education Act">Right to Education Act</a>. There was also a debate about removing caste-based reservation in favour of reservation based on income, a move supported by the RSS, but which was criticised as being discriminatory on the basis of caste.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEP_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-NEP-212">[211]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_Narendra_Modi" title="Foreign policy of Narendra Modi">Foreign policy of Narendra Modi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_prime_ministerial_trips_made_by_Narendra_Modi" title="List of prime ministerial trips made by Narendra Modi">List of prime ministerial trips made by Narendra Modi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="549" data-file-width="960" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg/220px-BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg/330px-BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg/440px-BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BRICS_leaders_meet_on_the_sidelines_of_2016_G20_Summit_in_China.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi with other BRICS leaders in 2016. Left to right: <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">Temer</a>, Modi, <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Putin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Zuma</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Foreign policy played a relatively small role in Modi's election campaign, and did not feature prominently in the BJP's election manifesto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2015_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2015-213">[212]</a></sup> Modi invited all the other leaders of <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">SAARC</a> countries to the ceremony where he was sworn in as prime minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grare_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grare-214">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pant_2014_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pant_2014-215">[214]</a></sup> He was the first Indian prime minister to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi's foreign policy, similarly to that of the preceding INC government, focused on improving economic ties, security, and regional relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2015_213-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2015-213">[212]</a></sup> Modi continued <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a>'s policy of "multialignment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2016_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2016-217">[216]</a></sup> The Modi administration tried to attract foreign investment in the Indian economy from several sources, especially in East Asia, with the use of slogans such as "Make in India" and "Digital India".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2016_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2016-217">[216]</a></sup> As a part of this policy, the Modi government completed India's application to join the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a>, which is led by China and Russia. (SCO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2016_217-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2016-217">[216]</a></sup> The government also tried to improve relations with Islamic republics in the Middle East, such as Bahrain, the Islamic Republic of Iran, Saudi Arabia, and the United Arab Emirates, as well as with Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2016_217-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2016-217">[216]</a></sup> Modi added five bilateral strategic partnerships to the 25 that had been agreed by his predecessors Singh and Vajpayee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2016_217-4"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2016-217">[216]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Modi-Obama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="650" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Modi-Obama.jpg/220px-Modi-Obama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Modi-Obama.jpg/330px-Modi-Obama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Modi-Obama.jpg/440px-Modi-Obama.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Modi-Obama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prime Minister Modi with President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> of the US, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the first few months after the election, Modi made trips to a number of different countries to further the goals of his policy, and attended the <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>, and <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> summits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2015_213-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2015-213">[212]</a></sup> One of Modi's first visits as prime minister was to Nepal, during which he promised a billion USD in aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mocko_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mocko-218">[217]</a></sup> Modi also made several overtures to the United States, including multiple visits to that country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pant_2014_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pant_2014-215">[214]</a></sup> While this was described as an unexpected development, due to the US having previously denied Modi a travel visa over his role during the 2002 Gujarat riots, it was also expected to strengthen diplomatic and trade relations between the two countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pant_2014_215-2"><a href="#cite_note-Pant_2014-215">[214]</a></sup> As of July 2016, Modi had made 51 trips to 42 countries with the intent of strengthening diplomatic relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, the Indian parliament ratified a land exchange deal with Bangladesh about the <a href="/wiki/India%E2%80%93Bangladesh_enclaves" title="India–Bangladesh enclaves">India–Bangladesh enclaves</a>, which had been initiated by the government of Manmohan Singh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronojoy_188-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ronojoy-188">[187]</a></sup> Modi's administration gave renewed attention to India's "Look East Policy", instituted in 1991. The policy was renamed the "Act East Policy", and involved directing Indian foreign policy towards <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_2016_217-5"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_2016-217">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Downie_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Downie-221">[220]</a></sup> The government signed agreements to improve land connectivity with <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, through the state of <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a>. This represented a break with India's historic engagement with Myanmar, which prioritized border security over trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Downie_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-Downie-221">[220]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence_policy">Defence policy</span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Indian_Prime_Minister_accuses_Pakistan_of_waging_proxy_war" title="wikinews:Indian Prime Minister accuses Pakistan of waging proxy war">Prime Minister Narendra Modi accuses Pakistan of waging proxy war.</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The BJP election manifesto had also promised to deal with illegal immigration into India in the Northeast, as well as to be more firm in its handling of insurgent groups. During the election campaign, Modi said that he would be willing to accommodate Hindu migrants who were being persecuted in Bangladesh, but those that came with "political objectives" would have to be sent back. The Modi government issued a notification allowing Hindu, Sikh, and Buddhist illegal immigrants from Pakistan and Bangladesh to legalise their residency in India. The government described the measure as being taken for humanitarian reasons but it drew criticism from several Assamese organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Northeast_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Northeast-222">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi continued the previous INC administration's policy of increasing military spending every year, announcing an increase of 11% in the military budget in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ladwig_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ladwig-223">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup> This increase was larger than the average growth under the Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ladwig_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ladwig-223">[222]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Modi administration negotiated a peace agreement with the largest faction of the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Council_of_Nagaland" title="National Socialist Council of Nagaland">National Socialist Council of Nagaland</a> (NSCM), which was announced in August 2015. The <a href="/wiki/Naga_people" title="Naga people">Naga</a> insurgency in northwest India had begun in the 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Northeast_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-Northeast-222">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinha_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sinha-225">[224]</a></sup> The NSCM and the government had agreed to a ceasefire in 1997, but a peace accord had not previously been signed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinha_225-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sinha-225">[224]</a></sup> In 2015 the government abrogated a 15-year ceasefire with the Khaplang faction of the NSCM (NSCM-K). The NSCM-K responded with a series of attacks, which killed 18 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Northeast_222-2"><a href="#cite_note-Northeast-222">[221]</a></sup> The Modi government carried out a raid across the border with Myanmar as a result, and labelled the NSCM-K a terrorist organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Northeast_222-3"><a href="#cite_note-Northeast-222">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi has repeatedly stated that <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> was an <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_and_state-sponsored_terrorism" title="Pakistan and state-sponsored terrorism">exporter of terrorism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tie0916_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-tie0916-226">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup> On 29 September 2016, the Indian Army stated that it had conducted a <a href="/wiki/Surgical_strike" title="Surgical strike">surgical strike</a> on terror launchpads in PoK,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> although Pakistan denied the claim, and the details of the confrontation are still in dispute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC2_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2-230">[229]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_policies">Environmental policies</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_(23193999974).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1412" data-file-width="2200" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_%2823193999974%29.jpg/220px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_%2823193999974%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_%2823193999974%29.jpg/330px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_%2823193999974%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_%2823193999974%29.jpg/440px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_%2823193999974%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_at_India_Pavilion_in_Paris_during_COP21_(23193999974).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi(right) at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CoP21_Climate_Conference" title="CoP21 Climate Conference">CoP21 Climate Conference</a>, in Paris, announcing the founding of an International <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_Alliance" title="Solar Alliance">Solar Alliance</a> (ISA). November 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In naming his cabinet, Modi renamed the "Ministry of Environment and Forests" the "Ministry of Environment, Forests, and Climate Change."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kothari_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kothari-231">[230]</a></sup> In the first budget of the government, the money allotted to this ministry was reduced by more than 50%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kothari_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kothari-231">[230]</a></sup> The new ministry also removed or diluted a number of laws related to environmental protection. These included no longer requiring clearance from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Board_for_Wildlife" title="National Board for Wildlife">National Board for Wildlife</a> for projects close to protected areas, and allowing certain projects to proceed before environmental clearance was received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-12"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kothari_231-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kothari-231">[230]</a></sup> The government also tried to reconstitute the Wildlife board such that it no longer had representatives from non-governmental organisations: however, this move was prevented by the Supreme court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kothari_231-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kothari-231">[230]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi also relaxed or abolished a number of other environmental regulations, particularly those related to industrial activity. A government committee stated that the existing system only served to create corruption, and that the government should instead rely on the owners of industries to voluntarily inform the government about the pollution they were creating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-13"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barry_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barry-232">[231]</a></sup> The changes were made with the aim of accelerating approval for industrial projects.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other changes included reducing ministry oversight on small mining projects, and no longer requiring approval from tribal councils for projects inside forested areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barry_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barry-232">[231]</a></sup> In addition, Modi lifted a moratorium on new industrial activity in the most polluted areas in the countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kothari_231-4"><a href="#cite_note-Kothari-231">[230]</a></sup> The changes were welcomed by businesspeople, but criticized by environmentalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barry_232-2"><a href="#cite_note-Barry-232">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under the UPA government that preceded Modi's administration, field trials of <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_food" title="Genetically modified food">Genetically Modified crops</a> had essentially put on hold, after protests from farmers fearing for their livelihoods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GM_crops_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-GM_crops-233">[232]</a></sup> Under the Modi government these restrictions were gradually lifted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GM_crops_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-GM_crops-233">[232]</a></sup> The government received some criticism for freezing the bank accounts of environmental group <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>, citing financial irregularities, although a leaked government report said that the freeze had to do with Greenpeace's opposition to GM crops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GM_crops_233-2"><a href="#cite_note-GM_crops-233">[232]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance_and_other_initiatives">Governance and other initiatives</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="299" data-file-width="684" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg/220px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg/330px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg/440px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_with_Chief_Ministers_in_December_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modi at the consultation meeting on replacing the Planning Commission with Chief Ministers of various states.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Modi's first year as prime minister saw significant centralization of power relative to previous administrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-8"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wyatt_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wyatt-234">[233]</a></sup> Modi's efforts at centralisation have been linked to an increase in the number of senior administration officials resigning their positions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-9"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> Although the government has a majority of seats in the Lok Sabha, it does not have one in the Rajya Sabha, which led to its policied frequently being stymied there. Thus, Modi resorted to passing a number of ordinances to enact his policies, leading to further centralisation of power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronojoy_188-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ronojoy-188">[187]</a></sup> The government also passed a bill increasing the control that it had over the appointment of judges, and reducing that of the judiciary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stepan_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-Stepan-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 December 2014, Modi announced that the <a href="/wiki/Planning_Commission_(India)" title="Planning Commission (India)">Planning Commission</a> had been scrapped. It was replaced with a body called the National Institution for Transforming India, or <a href="/wiki/NITI_Aayog" title="NITI Aayog">NITI Aayog</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_2015_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_2015-235">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sengupta_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sengupta-236">[235]</a></sup> The Planning Commission was a legacy of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Independence_movement" title="Indian Independence movement">Indian Independence movement</a>, although critics said that it was slowing economic growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patnaik_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-Patnaik-237">[236]</a></sup> The move had the effect of greatly centralizing the power previously with the planning commission in the person of the prime minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-14"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronojoy_188-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ronojoy-188">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_2015_235-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_2015-235">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sengupta_236-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sengupta-236">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patnaik_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-Patnaik-237">[236]</a></sup> It also reduced the extent of control individual states had over their financial allocation from the union government,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sengupta_236-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sengupta-236">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patnaik_237-2"><a href="#cite_note-Patnaik-237">[236]</a></sup> and unlike the planning commission, it does not have the power to allocate funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sengupta_236-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sengupta-236">[235]</a></sup> The planning commission had received heavy criticism in previous years for creating inefficiency in the government, and of not filling its role of improving social welfare: however, since the economic liberalisation of the 1990s, it had been the major government body responsible for measures related to social justice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sengupta_236-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sengupta-236">[235]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Modi government launched a crackdown against a number of civil society organisations. Several tens of thousands of organisations were investigated by the <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_Bureau_(India)" title="Intelligence Bureau (India)">Intelligence Bureau</a> in the first year of the administration, on the grounds that they were slowing economic growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-10"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> International <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian aid</a> organisation <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medecins_Sans_Frontieres" title="Medecins Sans Frontieres">Medecins Sans Frontieres</a> was among the groups that were put under pressure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-11"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> Other organisations affected included the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Club" title="Sierra Club">Sierra Club</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avaaz" title="Avaaz">Avaaz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruparelia_180-15"><a href="#cite_note-Ruparelia-180">[179]</a></sup> Cases of sedition were filed against individuals criticising the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-12"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup> This led to discontent with Modi's style of functioning within the BJP, and drew comparisons to the governing style of <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manor_113-13"><a href="#cite_note-Manor-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronojoy_188-5"><a href="#cite_note-Ronojoy-188">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi repealed 1,159 obsolete laws in first two years as prime minister, against a total of 1,301 such laws repealed by previous governments over a span of 64 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> He started a monthly radio program titled "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mann_ki_Baat" title="Mann ki Baat">Mann ki Baat</a>" on 3 October 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> Modi also launched the <a href="/wiki/Digital_India" title="Digital India">Digital India</a> programme, which has the goal of ensuring that government services are available electronically, building infrastructure so rural areas get high-speed Internet access, boosting manufacturing of electronic goods in the country, and promoting <a href="/wiki/Digital_literacy" title="Digital literacy">digital literacy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[242]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>In accordance with Ghanchi tradition, Modi's marriage was arranged by his parents when he was a child. He was engaged at age 13 to <a href="/wiki/Jashodaben" title="Jashodaben">Jashodaben</a>, marrying her when he was 18. They spent little time together and grew apart when Modi began two years of travel, including visits to Hindu <a href="/wiki/Ashram" title="Ashram">ashrams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jose_Caravan_21-6"><a href="#cite_note-Jose_Caravan-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[243]</a></sup> Reportedly, their marriage was never <a href="/wiki/Consummation" title="Consummation">consummated</a> and he kept it a secret because otherwise he could not have become a 'pracharak' in the puritan Rashtriya Swayamsewak Sangh (RSS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013A_time_of_difference_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukhopadhyay2013A_time_of_difference-245">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IT13092013_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-IT13092013-44">[44]</a></sup> Although Modi kept his marriage secret for most of his career, he acknowledged his wife when he filed his nomination for a parliamentary seat in the 2014 general elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[246]</a></sup> Modi maintains a close relationship with his mother, Hiraben and often visits her on his birthday to seek her blessings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Image"><span id="Personality_and_image"></span>Image</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_image_of_Narendra_Modi" title="Public image of Narendra Modi">Public image of Narendra Modi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_(24408800864).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1473" data-file-width="2200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_%2824408800864%29.jpg/220px-PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_%2824408800864%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_%2824408800864%29.jpg/330px-PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_%2824408800864%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_%2824408800864%29.jpg/440px-PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_%2824408800864%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PM_Modi_greets_people_in_Visakhapatnam_(24408800864).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
PM Modi greets people in <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Vegetarianism" title="Vegetarianism">vegetarian</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[248]</a></sup> Modi has a frugal lifestyle and is a <a href="/wiki/Workaholic" title="Workaholic">workaholic</a> and introvert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup> Adept at using social media, he has been since September 2014 the second-most-followed leader in the world (with over 25.8 million followers on Twitter as of December 2016), behind only <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wpSocialMedia_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-wpSocialMedia-166">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup> Modi's 31 August 2012 post on Google Hangouts made him the first Indian politician to interact with <a href="/wiki/Netizen" title="Netizen">netizens</a> on live chat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-toi-253">[252]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibn_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibn-254">[253]</a></sup></p>
<p>Modi has also been called a fashion-icon with his signature, crisply ironed, half-sleeved tunic-shirt (dubbed the "Modi <a href="/wiki/Kurta" title="Kurta">kurta</a>"), brand-name accessories, and a suit with his name embroidered repeatedly in the pinstripes that he wore during a state visit by US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, drawing particular public and media attention, and sometimes criticism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sharma_June_2014_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma_June_2014-255">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Friedman_June_2014_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-Friedman_June_2014-256">[255]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price-257">[256]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although he is considered a controversial, polarising and divisive figure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[257]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[259]</a></sup> British economist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jim_O%27Neill_(economist)" title="Jim O'Neill (economist)">Jim O'Neill</a> blogged that Modi is "good on economics" – one of the things "India desperately needs in a leader".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-et20130715_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-et20130715-261">[260]</a></sup> In August 2013, financial analyst <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wood_(financial_analyst)" title="Christopher Wood (financial analyst)">Chris Wood</a> of <a href="/wiki/CLSA" title="CLSA">CLSA</a> wrote in his weekly "Greed &amp; fear" report: "The Indian stock market's greatest hope is the emergence of Gujarat Chief Minister Narendra Modi as the BJP's prime ministerial candidate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-et20130715_261-1"><a href="#cite_note-et20130715-261">[260]</a></sup></p>
<p>As prime minister, Modi has received consistently high approval ratings; at the end of his first year in office, he received an overall approval rating of 87% in a Pew Research poll, with 68% of people rating him "very favorably" and 93% approving of his government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup> His approval rating remained largely consistent at around 74% through his second year in office, according to a nationwide poll conducted by instaVaani.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[262]</a></sup> At the end of his second year in office, an updated Pew Research poll showed Modi continued to receive high overall approval ratings of 81%, with 57% of those polled rating him "very favorably."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[264]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span></h2>
<p>In 2001, Modi co-authored <i>Setubandh</i>, a biography of the RSS leader <a href="/wiki/Lakshmanrao_Inamdar" title="Lakshmanrao Inamdar">Lakshmanrao Inamdar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[265]</a></sup> In 2007, a collection of Modi's poems was published as a book titled <i>Aankh Aa Dhanya Chhe</i> (Our Eyes Are So Blessed) .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[266]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[267]</a></sup> Modi also authored <i>Karmayog</i>, a 101-page booklet discussing manual scavenging. In it, Modi argued that scavenging was a "spiritual experience" for <a href="/wiki/Dalit" title="Dalit">Dalits</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[270]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[271]</a></sup> However, this book was not circulated that time because of election code of conduct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[272]</a></sup> His Gujarati book titled <i>Jyotipunj</i> was published in 2008. The book contained biographical profiles of various RSS leaders that had inspired Modi. The longest profile was of <a href="/wiki/M._S._Golwalkar" title="M. S. Golwalkar">M. S. Golwalkar</a>, under whose leadership the RSS expanded and whom Modi refers to as <i>Pujniya Shri Guruji</i> ("Guru worthy of worship").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[273]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economic_Times" title="The Economic Times">The Economic Times</a></i>, his intention was to explain the workings of the RSS to his readers and to reassure RSS members that he remained ideologically sound. Modi has authored eight other books, mostly containing short stories for children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[274]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_recognition">Awards and recognition</span></h2>
<p>Modi was named Best Chief Minister in a 2007 nationwide survey by <i><a href="/wiki/India_Today" title="India Today">India Today</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[275]</a></sup> In March 2012, he appeared on the cover of the Asian edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i>, one of the few Indian politicians to have done so,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[276]</a></sup> He was awarded <a href="/wiki/CNN-IBN_Indian_of_the_Year" title="CNN-IBN Indian of the Year">Indian of the Year</a> by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNN-IBN" title="CNN-IBN">CNN-IBN</a></i> news network in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[277]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014 and 2015, he was named one of Time magazine's <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100 Most Influential People in the World</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[278]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[279]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[280]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[281]</a></sup> He was also declared winner of the Time magazine reader's poll for <a href="/wiki/Time_Person_of_the_Year" title="Time Person of the Year">Person of the Year</a> in 2014, a feat which he repeated again in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[282]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[283]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forbes_Magazine" title="Forbes Magazine">Forbes Magazine</a></i> ranked him the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_list_of_The_World%27s_Most_Powerful_People" title="Forbes list of The World's Most Powerful People">15th-Most-Powerful Person in the World</a> in 2014 and the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_list_of_The_World%27s_Most_Powerful_People" title="Forbes list of The World's Most Powerful People">9th-Most-Powerful Person in the World</a> in 2015 and 2016 again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[284]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[285]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[286]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[287]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Modi was one of <i>Time</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s "30 Most Influential People on the Internet" as the second-most-followed politician on Twitter and Facebook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[288]</a></sup> In the same year he was ranked fifth on <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune Magazine</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s first annual list of "World's Greatest Leaders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[289]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[290]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Citations">Citations</span></h3>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Bye-election</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-even hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
